## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Registration and Execution

## Your Task

Trace how HTTP filter chains are registered and executed in the Envoy proxy. Find C++ and protobuf files across envoyproxy/envoy and envoyproxy/data-plane-api that implement: the FilterChainFactory interface (in envoy/http/), the FilterChainHelper that constructs chains from config, the FilterManager that executes filter chains at runtime, and the HttpConnectionManager proto that defines the filter_chain configuration schema.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

## Summary

I've traced the HTTP filter chain registration and execution in Envoy across both the `envoy--v1.31.2` and `data-plane-api--84e84367` repositories. The answer includes:

### Key Findings:

1. **FilterChainFactory Interface** (`envoy/http/filter_factory.h`): Defines the contract for creating HTTP filter chains with methods `createFilterChain()` and `createUpgradeFilterChain()`.

2. **FilterChainHelper** (`source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h`): A template class that processes HTTP filter configurations at startup, converting protobuf filter specifications into filter factory callbacks.

3. **HttpConnectionManager Proto** (`http_connection_manager.proto`): Defines the configuration schema with a `repeated HttpFilter http_filters` field that specifies which filters to apply.

4. **HttpConnectionManagerConfig** (`config.h/cc`): Implements FilterChainFactory, processes configuration during construction using FilterChainHelper, and stores pre-instantiated filter factories.

5. **FilterManager** (`filter_manager.h/cc`): Executes the filter chain at runtime, handling data flow through decoder and encoder filter chains.

6. **ConnectionManagerImpl** (`conn_manager_impl.cc`): Creates new ActiveStreams when HTTP requests arrive, each with its own FilterManager instance.

### Execution Flow:
- **Configuration Time**: HttpConnectionManagerConfig uses FilterChainHelper to process http_filters from protobuf and stores filter factory callbacks
- **Runtime**: ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream() creates ActiveStream with FilterManager → FilterManager::createFilterChain() → calls FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain() → applies stored filter factories →

For each filter, `FilterChainHelper::processFilter()` (lines 105-165) performs dependency validation, instantiates the appropriate filter factory based on the registered filter name, calls the factory's `createFilterFactoryFromProto()` method to create a `FilterFactoryCb` (a callback function that creates filter instances), and stores it in a list of filter factories. These factories are stored in `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::filter_factories_` for the main HTTP filter chain.\\n\\n## Upgrade Filter Chains\\nFor HTTP upgrade scenarios (like WebSocket), separate filter chains can be configured. The `HttpConnectionManager::upgrade_configs` field allows per-upgrade-type filter chains. These are processed similarly by `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` and stored in `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::upgrade_filter_factories_` as a map keyed by upgrade type (config.cc, lines 717-743).\\n\\n## Runtime Filter Chain Creation\\nAt runtime, when a new HTTP stream arrives:\\n\\n1. The `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` method (conn_manager_impl.cc, lines 378-427) is called by the underlying codec when a new request headers frame arrives.\\n\\n2. The FilterManager is passed a reference to the `FilterChainFactory` (the `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` instance) from `connection_manager_.config_->filterFactory()`.\\n\\n3. The FilterManager also receives the filter chain options and creates access log handlers from the configuration.\\n\\n4. When the first request headers are received and decoded by the HTTP codec, the stream decoding process begins. The `ActiveStream` eventually calls `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` (filter_manager.cc, lines 1550-1586).\\n\\n## Filter Chain Execution\\nThe `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` method checks if an upgrade header exists. If it does, it calls `FilterChainFactory::createUpgradeFilterChain()` (the HttpConnectionManagerConfig's override), which looks up the upgrade type in the upgrade factories and applies those filters. If no upgrade or upgrade creation fails, it calls `FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` (lines 1584), which is implemented in HttpConnectionManagerConfig (config.cc, lines 780-784).\\n\\nThe `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain()` method calls `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` with the stored `filter_factories_` list. This utility function iterates through each stored filter factory and calls `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()` (filter_manager.cc, lines 551-554) for each one. This creates a `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl` object and invokes the stored `FilterFactoryCb`, which instantiates the actual filter instance and registers it with the FilterManager via callbacks like `addStreamDecoderFilter()` or `addStreamEncoderFilter()`.\\n\\nOnce the filter chain is created, as request data arrives (headers, body, trailers), the FilterManager drives data through the decoder filter chain via `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, and `decodeTrailers()` methods (filter_manager.cc, lines 569+). Each filter in the chain processes the data in order, and filters can stop iteration to perform asynchronous work before continuing. Response data flows through the encoder filter chain in reverse order.\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n- **Factory Pattern**: Filter factories are registered globally and looked up by name during configuration.\\n- **Callback Chain**: Filter factory callbacks capture filter construction logic; when invoked, they instantiate the actual filter.\\n- **Manager Pattern**: The FilterManager orchestrates data flow through the filters, maintaining iteration state and handling filter callbacks.\\n- **Configuration Providers**: Both static (configuration-time created) and dynamic (loaded via xDS) filter configurations are supported via `FilterConfigProvider` abstractions.\\n\\nThis architecture allows Envoy to support dynamic filter configuration updates (ECDS), route-based filter disabling, and complex filter dependencies while maintaining a clean separation between configuration and runtime execution.\"\n}\n",

If no upgrade or upgrade creation fails, it calls `FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` (lines 1584), which is implemented in HttpConnectionManagerConfig (config.cc, lines 780-784).\\n\\nThe `HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain()` method calls `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` with the stored `filter_factories_` list. This utility function iterates through each stored filter factory and calls `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()` (filter_manager.cc, lines 551-554) for each one. This creates a `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl` object and invokes the stored `FilterFactoryCb`, which instantiates the actual filter instance and registers it with the FilterManager via callbacks like `addStreamDecoderFilter()` or `addStreamEncoderFilter()`.\\n\\nOnce the filter chain is created, as request data arrives (headers, body, trailers), the FilterManager drives data through the decoder filter chain via `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, and `decodeTrailers()` methods (filter_manager.cc, lines 569+). Each filter in the chain processes the data in order, and filters can stop iteration to perform asynchronous work before continuing. Response data flows through the encoder filter chain in reverse order.\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n- **Factory Pattern**: Filter factories are registered globally and looked up by name during configuration.\\n- **Callback Chain**: Filter factory callbacks capture filter construction logic; when invoked, they instantiate the actual filter.\\n- **Manager Pattern**: The FilterManager orchestrates data flow through the filters, maintaining iteration state and handling filter callbacks.\\n- **Configuration Providers**: Both static (configuration-time created) and dynamic (loaded via xDS) filter configurations are supported via `FilterConfigProvider` abstractions.\\n\\nThis architecture allows Envoy to support dynamic filter configuration updates (ECDS), route-based filter disabling, and complex filter dependencies while maintaining a clean separation between configuration and runtime execution.\"\n}\n",
